  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>Working on an Android application using Orekit, I've discovered that a simple FastMath.floor() takes about 4 to 5 secs on a 1GHz Nexus One phone (only the first time it's called). I've launched the Android profiling tool (traceview) and the problem seems to be linked with the static portion of FastMath code named "// Initialize tables"</p> 
                  <p>The timing resulted in :</p> 
                  <ul class="alternate" type="square"> 
                   <li>FastMath.slowexp (40.8%)</li> 
                   <li>FastMath.expint (39.2%)<br> - FastMath.quadmult() (95.6% of expint)</li> 
                   <li>FastMath.slowlog (18.2%)</li> 
                  </ul> 
                  <p>Hoping that would help</p> 
                  <p>Thanks!</p> 
                  <p>Alexis Robert</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

Sebb\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13090224_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'24\\/Aug\\/11 13:49\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2011-08-24T13:49:51+0000\'\u003e24\\/Aug\\/11 13:49\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eAny change needs to bear in mind that the fields need to remain thread-safe, i.e. whatever generates them must publish the values safely to all threads. This is currently achieved by using the static{} block with final fields.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSeems to me there are two possible approaches to fix this:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eimprove the performance of the existing code\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003echange the code to use initialisation on demand, so only the required parts are intialised.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nStatic holder classes can probably be used here to ensure safe publication.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIn the case of floor(), that does not need the calculated fields, so it would speed it up.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eNote that the FastMath version of floor() is likely to have similar performance to Math.floor(), as it\'s not an algorithm that benefits from (or indeed needs) the FastMath approach.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIt would be useful to have performance figures for more complicated calculations, where FastMath should start to show benefits.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"sebb@apache.org\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13090224_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=sebb%40apache.org\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"sebb@apache.org\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Sebb\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13090224_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'24\\/Aug\\/11 13:49\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2011-08-24T13:49:51+0000\'\u003e24\\/Aug\\/11 13:49\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Any change needs to bear in mind that the fields need to remain thread-safe, i.e. whatever generates them must publish the values safely to all threads. This is currently achieved by using the static{} block with final fields. \\n\\n Seems to me there are two possible approaches to fix this: \\n \\n\\t improve the performance of the existing code \\n\\t change the code to use initialisation on demand, so only the required parts are intialised. \\nStatic holder classes can probably be used here to ensure safe publication. \\n \\n\\n\\n In the case of floor(), that does not need the calculated fields, so it would speed it up. \\n\\n Note that the FastMath version of floor() is likely to have similar performance to Math.floor(), as it\'s not an algorithm that benefits from (or indeed needs) the FastMath approach. \\n\\n It would be useful to have performance figures for more complicated calculations, where FastMath should start to show benefits.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-13090294\\\" datetime=\'2011-09-07T22:48:05+0000\'\u003e07\\/Sep\\/11 22:48\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eIIUC, only the initializations needed by a method call are performed.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nThus \\\"max\\\" has become fast because it doesn\'t need any of those data arrays.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFor those methods that need the data, one has to compare the startup times between computing the data and loading precomputed data. For methods that only need some of the data, the time gain might not be worth trailing the huge precomputed arrays.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf several calls are made to methods that need most of the data arrays, the initialization time will be increasingly negligible (with respect to the \\\"useful\\\" application running time). Which again renders the precomputed arrays unnecessary.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo, in summary, lazy initialization is very nice, especially for short-lived applications that happen to call methods that don\'t need the data at all.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nIt\'s still nice for applications that happen to need only part of the data.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nIt\'s useless for applications that will need all the data arrays. (But it probably does not hurt.)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nHowever, I still don\'t see an advantage in storing precomputed values. I don\'t think that it should be adopted just for a toy application that would call a math function once and exit.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"erans\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13099632_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=erans\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"erans\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Gilles\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13099632_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'07\\/Sep\\/11 22:48\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2011-09-07T22:48:05+0000\'\u003e07\\/Sep\\/11 22:48\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    IIUC, only the initializations needed by a method call are performed. \\nThus \\\"max\\\" has become fast because it doesn\'t need any of those data arrays. \\n\\n For those methods that need the data, one has to compare the startup times between computing the data and loading precomputed data. For methods that only need some of the data, the time gain might not be worth trailing the huge precomputed arrays. \\n\\n If several calls are made to methods that need most of the data arrays, the initialization time will be increasingly negligible (with respect to the \\\"useful\\\" application running time). Which again renders the precomputed arrays unnecessary. \\n\\n So, in summary, lazy initialization is very nice, especially for short-lived applications that happen to call methods that don\'t need the data at all. \\nIt\'s still nice for applications that happen to need only part of the data. \\nIt\'s useless for applications that will need all the data arrays. (But it probably does not hurt.) \\nHowever, I still don\'t see an advantage in storing precomputed values. I don\'t think that it should be adopted just for a toy application that would call a math function once and exit.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \\n\\n Tidying up the code to move the now-unused init code makes only a minor improvement to load times, but is worth it for readability and maintenance. \\n\\n You can do the tests if you want. \\nMath 2.2 is the original FastMath implementation \\n\\n  https:\\/\\/repository.apache.org\\/content\\/repositories\\/snapshots\\/org\\/apache\\/commons\\/commons-math\\/3.0-SNAPSHOT\\/  \\nhas the jars: \\ncommons-math-3.0-20110907.123252-61.jar - preset arrays \\ncommons-math-3.0-20110907.222813-62.jar - the IOD code \\n\\n So yes, if an application makes lots of calls the overhead will gradually fade away, but the overhead is very large. \\nIn my test I used exp(1000) which uses an IOD table.  \\nThe repeat time for that is about 5000ns. \\nThe first times are approx 40,000,000ns (original) and 8,000,000ns (current). \\n\\n I agree that the lazy init does not help applications that use all the tables. \\nHowever all applications perform better if the table calculation is done beforehand.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-13100221\\\" I\'ve done a little timing test which is this simple Java code :\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"preformatted panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"preformattedContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre\u003e \\nimport org.apache.commons.math.util.FastMath;\\n\\npublic class Timing {\\n\\tpublic static void main(String[] args) {\\n\\t\\tlong start = 0, stop = 0;\\n\\t\\t\\n\\t\\tstart = System.nanoTime();\\n\\t\\tFastMath.pow(2, 64);\\n\\t\\tstop = System.nanoTime();\\n\\t\\t\\n\\t\\tSystem.out.printf(\\\"time = %f ms\\\\n\\\", (float)((stop-start)\\/1000000.0));\\n\\t}\\n}\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'ve launched this program both on my phone and on my laptop (Intel(R) Core(TM)2 Duo CPU T8100 2.10GHz, Linux 3.0, J2SE 1.7.0-b147), and I get the following results.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eUSE_PRECOMPUTED_TABLES = true (r1169543) :\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eComputer : time = 33.472633 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ePhone : time = 12.847901 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eUSE_PRECOMPUTED_TABLES = false (r1169543) :\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eComputer : time = 79.367081 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ePhone : time = 317.840576 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOld version before the bug report (r1160914 &#8211; 2011-08-24 00:35:06) :\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul class=\\\"alternate\\\" type=\\\"square\\\"\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eComputer : time = 114.170425 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ePhone : time = 3518.310547 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe thing is that we must consider the fact that Android use an other virtual machine which have really different bytecodes (even in structure, dalvik bytecode is register based), have a different JIT (DalvikVM use a trace based JIT, and iirc Hotspot has a method based JIT), and iirc they also have a different implementation of the standard library (Android use Apache Harmony). So the fact that we may have slightly lower results on a phone on one use case with such low timings doesn\'t seem me so strange.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBy the way, you asked for the use case. I\'m developing an Android application using Orekit so the user can have access to often used spatial dynamics computations right from its pocket, like a specialized handheld calculator. These 4s is the time which the user has to wait with a \\\"Please wait ...\\\" dialog, instead of having a instantaneous result (which the user expects &#8211; users are often more exigent for the loading time on a phone than on a computer, that\'s completely psychological). That\'s even worse when there is additional data loading or computations, where those 4s have to be added to the data loading\\/computation time. A response time with the magnitude of 100ms is really perfect !\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"ale6\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13107256_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=ale6\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"ale6\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Alexis Robert\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13107256_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'17\\/Sep\\/11 20:57\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2011-09-17T20:57:49+0000\'\u003e17\\/Sep\\/11 20:57\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Hmm, you\'re right, if I understood correctly we were timing with different method (I was timing with the Android profiler). I\'ve done a little timing test which is this simple Java code : \\n\\n  \\n  \\nimport org.apache.commons.math.util.FastMath;\\n\\npublic class Timing {\\n\\tpublic static void main(String[] args) {\\n\\t\\tlong start = 0, stop = 0;\\n\\t\\t\\n\\t\\tstart = System.nanoTime();\\n\\t\\tFastMath.pow(2, 64);\\n\\t\\tstop = System.nanoTime();\\n\\t\\t\\n\\t\\tSystem.out.printf(\\\"time = %f ms\\\\n\\\", (float)((stop-start)\\/1000000.0));\\n\\t}\\n}\\n \\n  \\n\\n I\'ve launched this program both on my phone and on my laptop (Intel(R) Core(TM)2 Duo CPU T8100 2.10GHz, Linux 3.0, J2SE 1.7.0-b147), and I get the following results. \\n\\n USE_PRECOMPUTED_TABLES = true (r1169543) : \\n \\n\\t Computer : time = 33.472633 ms \\n\\t Phone : time = 12.847901 ms \\n \\n\\n\\n USE_PRECOMPUTED_TABLES = false (r1169543) : \\n \\n\\t Computer : time = 79.367081 ms \\n\\t Phone : time = 317.840576 ms \\n \\n\\n\\n Old version before the bug report (r1160914 &#8211; 2011-08-24 00:35:06) : \\n \\n\\t Computer : time = 114.170425 ms \\n\\t Phone : time = 3518.310547 ms \\n \\n\\n\\n The thing is that we must consider the fact that Android use an other virtual machine which have really different bytecodes (even in structure, dalvik bytecode is register based), have a different JIT (DalvikVM use a trace based JIT, and iirc Hotspot has a method based JIT), and iirc they also have a different implementation of the standard library (Android use Apache Harmony). So the fact that we may have slightly lower results on a phone on one use case with such low timings doesn\'t seem me so strange. \\n\\n By the way, you asked for the use case. I\'m developing an Android application using Orekit so the user can have access to often used spatial dynamics computations right from its pocket, like a specialized handheld calculator. These 4s is the time which the user has to wait with a \\\"Please wait ...\\\" dialog, instead of having a instantaneous result (which the user expects &#8211; users are often more exigent for the loading time on a phone than on a computer, that\'s completely psychological). That\'s even worse when there is additional data loading or computations, where those 4s have to be added to the data loading\\/computation time. A response time with the magnitude of 100ms is really perfect !              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n It requires additional supporting code, the data files are not readable, and is not always as fast as the arrays. fixed for the static array case by using element getters rather than providing access to the entire arrays. \\nIf this proves workable performance-wise, that would be just as good for me as the original local arrays. \\nMy second choice is external arrays with direct access rather than getters (as is done at present).              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n Literal arrays (or loading from resources) reduce the delay but the big gain was through IOD. \u003cem\u003eThat part\u003c\\/em\u003e should have closed this specific issue, not the additional pre-computation \\\"feature\\\".\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nIMHO, the literal arrays (or resources) trick is a temporary workaround, until it is clear for all that the time gain has become insignificant (and the \\\"RECOMPUTE_TABLES_AT_RUNTIME\\\" can be used again).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe \\\"resources\\\" solution may not be ideal, but neither is the literal arrays one; we have divergent listings of what is more important.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nAs for the technical limitations which you point out, maybe that they can be lifted, and if so it could even also improve the efficiency of that alternative.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI can never agree that using literal arrays is the right way to deal with pre-computed data. Literal arrays (or loading from resources) reduce the delay but the big gain was through IOD.  That part  should have closed this specific issue, not the additional pre-computation \\\"feature\\\". \\nIMHO, the literal arrays (or resources) trick is a temporary workaround, until it is clear for all that the time gain has become insignificant (and the \\\"RECOMPUTE_TABLES_AT_RUNTIME\\\" can be used again). \\n\\n The \\\"resources\\\" solution may not be ideal, but neither is the literal arrays one; we have divergent listings of what is more important. \\nAs for the technical limitations which you point out, maybe that they can be lifted, and if so it could even also improve the efficiency of that alternative. \\n\\n I can never agree that using literal arrays is the right way to deal with pre-computed data. If it were so, what would be resources for? \\n\\n Getting 3.0 out is more important than fighting over this, so I\'ll drop the case. \\n\\n For \\\"more security\\\" with the literal arrays, you can just add a call to \\\"clone\\\" instead of returning a reference to the internal arrays in \\\"FastMasthLiteralArrays\\\". This will create an additional copy but is likely to be faster than a sequence of getter calls (although this is again a trade-off likely to be below the significance level of most applications...). added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13204559_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'09\\/Feb\\/12 14:50\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2012-02-09T14:50:10+0000\'\u003e09\\/Feb\\/12 14:50\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI finally succeeded in running on my tablet a slightly modified version of Gilles test (thanks for putting this together Gilles). The test involves computing 1abs, 10 floor, 30 sin, 30 cos, 50 sqrt, 5 exp, 2 log which is representative of the small application we developed. The results shown represent the time for all computation, using only FastMath methods. The tests were run 10 times, with a fresh start each time.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAndroid tablet, Nvidia Tegra2 chipset at 1GHz, 1Gb memory, running Android 3.0.1:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eliteral arrays:    mean  35.1 ms, standard deviation 0.658 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eresources loading: mean  55.2 ms, standard deviation 0.651 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003etable computation: mean 155.4 ms, standard deviation 0.850 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eDesktop computer, quadcore AMD phenom 9550 quadcore 64 bits at 2.2 GHz, 6 Gb memore, running Debian Linux wheezy with OpenJDK 6 20.0b12:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eliteral arrays:    mean  71.4 ms, standard deviation 0.449 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eresources loading: mean  70.3 ms, standard deviation 1.731 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003etable computation: mean 132.9 ms, standard deviation 1.661 ms\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThese results show that on the Android platform, the gain from precomputed tables is much larger than on the desktop. In fact, the test runs at least twice faster on Android than on the desktop for precomputed table, and 17% slower when tables are computed at startup.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe difference between literal arrays and resources slightly favors literal arrays on the Android platforms, but on desktop the difference is below standard deviation. In any case, it is quite small (20 ms) and therefore not significant as it is a one time startup cost only.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo I would conclude that precomputing the tables is a worthwhile improvement.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eNow considering how pre-computed tables should be set up, I have no clear cut opinion. I would like to not have the tables in the source distribution and have them generated automatically at build time. It seems to me maven does have both generate-source and generate-resource goals in its lifecycle, but these goals are triggered only by specific plugins (antlr, build-helper, ...). These plugins are not suitable for our case which merely consist in compiling a first standalone class, then run it to build either the java file or the resource file.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAny ideas about that ? \u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"luc\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13204559_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=luc\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"luc\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Luc Maisonobe\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13204559_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'09\\/Feb\\/12 14:50\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2012-02-09T14:50:10+0000\'\u003e09\\/Feb\\/12 14:50\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I finally succeeded in running on my tablet a slightly modified version of Gilles test (thanks for putting this together Gilles). The test involves computing 1abs, 10 floor, 30 sin, 30 cos, 50 sqrt, 5 exp, 2 log which is representative of the small application we developed. The results shown represent the time for all computation, using only FastMath methods. The tests were run 10 times, with a fresh start each time. \\n\\n Android tablet, Nvidia Tegra2 chipset at 1GHz, 1Gb memory, running Android 3.0.1: \\n \\n\\t literal arrays:    mean  35.1 ms, standard deviation 0.658 ms \\n\\t resources loading: mean  55.2 ms, standard deviation 0.651 ms \\n\\t table computation: mean 155.4 ms, standard deviation 0.850 ms \\n \\n\\n\\n Desktop computer, quadcore AMD phenom 9550 quadcore 64 bits at 2.2 GHz, 6 Gb memore, running Debian Linux wheezy with OpenJDK 6 20.0b12: \\n \\n\\t literal arrays:    mean  71.4 ms, standard deviation 0.449 ms \\n\\t resources loading: mean  70.3 ms, standard deviation 1.731 ms \\n\\t table computation: mean 132.9 ms, standard deviation 1.661 ms \\n \\n\\n\\n These results show that on the Android platform, the gain from precomputed tables is much larger than on the desktop. In fact, the test runs at least twice faster on Android than on the desktop for precomputed table, and 17% slower when tables are computed at startup. \\n\\n The difference between literal arrays and resources slightly favors literal arrays on the Android platforms, but on desktop the difference is below standard deviation. In any case, it is quite small (20 ms) and therefore not significant as it is a one time startup cost only. \\n\\n So I would conclude that precomputing the tables is a worthwhile improvement. \\n\\n Now considering how pre-computed tables should be set up, I have no clear cut opinion. I would like to not have the tables in the source distribution and have them generated automatically at build time. It seems to me maven does have both generate-source and generate-resource goals in its lifecycle, but these goals are triggered only by specific plugins (antlr, build-helper, ...). These plugins are not suitable for our case which merely consist in compiling a first standalone class, then run it to build either the java file or the resource file. \\n\\n Any ideas about that ? pre-computed tables are loaded. We have two competing implementations for that: resources loaded from a binary file and literal arrays compiled in the library. In both cases, the data is generated beforehand by our own code, so in both case users who wants to re-generate them with different settings can do so.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe advantages of resources are that they are more compact (binary) and don\'t clutter the sources with large tables.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nThe advantages of literal arrays are that the can be checked by mere human beings and don\'t require any support code.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nThe speed difference between the two implementation exists but is tiny.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eTwo people have already expressed their preferences (one favoring resources the other one favoring literal arrays). I don\'t have a clear cut preference myself (only a slight bias toward one solution which I prefer to keep for myself).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI would like to have the opinions of newer developers and users on this before selecting one approach. We have two competing implementations for that: resources loaded from a binary file and literal arrays compiled in the library. In both cases, the data is generated beforehand by our own code, so in both case users who wants to re-generate them with different settings can do so. \\n\\n The advantages of resources are that they are more compact (binary) and don\'t clutter the sources with large tables. \\nThe advantages of literal arrays are that the can be checked by mere human beings and don\'t require any support code. \\nThe speed difference between the two implementation exists but is tiny. \\n\\n Two people have already expressed their preferences (one favoring resources the other one favoring literal arrays). I don\'t have a clear cut preference myself (only a slight bias toward one solution which I prefer to keep for myself). \\n\\n I would like to have the opinions of newer developers and users on this before selecting one approach. Could someone please provide another opinion ?              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-13206119\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/MATH-650?focusedCommentId=13206119&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-13206119\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"celestin\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13206119_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=celestin\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"celestin\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e S\\u00E9bastien Brisard\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13206119_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'11\\/Feb\\/12 13:44\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2012-02-11T13:44:58+0000\'\u003e11\\/Feb\\/12 13:44\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eHi Luc,\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nthanks for taking care of this difficult issue. I would lean on the binary side, for \\\"safety\\\" reasons: unwanted modifications are less likely to occur. But I do realize that this can be endlessly debated over, and to be really honnest, I would be very happy with either solution (or even the runtime computation: as far as I am concerned, the typical timing of my computations is about 1 hour to one week... plenty of seconds...).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nIf we opt for the binary option, maybe we could provide a binary-to-ascii method, for anyone to check the data (maybe that\'s already available).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nI\'m surprised though that binary files take longer to load than litteral. I should have thought that reading a presumably longer table, and parsing a presumably larger number of octets for each double would result in a longer loading time.
